    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1876576184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1876576184" />
    <a title="Esme" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44110461-esme"><img alt="Esme" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1876576184?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Esme" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Esme" href="/user/show/44110461-esme">Esme</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1876576184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1609866328394206437">I can’t get enough of this series, it’s a problem. I don’t know what I’m going to do with myself when I finish all of the stand alones, which is coming up fast. I burned through this one on the audiobook version – and didn’t take notes. Please forgive names that are spelled wrong. If you haven’t read First Law trilogy yet, I’d absolutely say start there.<br/><br/>Plot:<br/>More war, such is life in the First Law world, this one has some crossover characters from some of the other books. Black Dow is King of th</span>
  <span id="freeText1609866328394206437" style="display:none">I can’t get enough of this series, it’s a problem. I don’t know what I’m going to do with myself when I finish all of the stand alones, which is coming up fast. I burned through this one on the audiobook version – and didn’t take notes. Please forgive names that are spelled wrong. If you haven’t read First Law trilogy yet, I’d absolutely say start there.<br /><br />Plot:<br />More war, such is life in the First Law world, this one has some crossover characters from some of the other books. Black Dow is King of the North now, and he’s not any more of a peaceful leader than his predecessor was, he’s waging war against the Union and it’s proving to be a tough fight.<br /><br />This book had fewer plot threads than the first trilogy, or at least it felt that way to me. It’s pretty straightforward, The Union is pitted against the Northmen, and neither side has much of a clear advantage. As soon as one side has a battle victory, the next day’s victory is claimed by the other side.<br /><br />This is more about showing the atrocities of warfare, a lot of the first trilogy was spent building up, there were skirmishes and fights in The Blade Itself, but the war didn’t come until later. This book is basically one long battle, the entire thing takes place in just about a weeks worth of time, but a lot of action happens within that time period.<br /><br />We watch a bunch of different characters viewpoints from both sides of the war having it out and trying to win the day.<br /><br />A young boy named Beck is trying to earn his name in some great battle, he’s left his family’s farm behind determined to walk in his fathers’ footsteps – who was also a famous warrior in the north.<br /><br />A disgraced officer named Tunny who would rather laze around than fight is begrudgingly teaching new recruits “how to be soldiers”, and he hates it.<br /><br />We also follow Gorst, who was seen in the first trilogy is madly in love with a generals daughter, who herself is married to an officer in the army. Gorst is bitter and resentful towards his position in the army, writing angry letters in the night to the king, then burning them as some sort of therapy.<br /><br />The general’s daughter, Finree, is also featured and she’s trying her best to hoist her husband higher and higher in the army. He’s the son of a traitor and has to scrape his way to every promotion, he works himself twice as hard as anyone else trying his best to prove he’s no traitor. She’s a very gung ho and ambitious person who speaks up often, which grates on the patience of First Magi Bayaz and other higher-ups in the military – it causes some problems.<br /><br />Craw is fighting for the north, and he’s one of the last “straight edges” left, meaning he regards honor as much or more than just brute strength in a fight. He’s trying to be a better man and lead people into doing the right thing even if it doesn’t get you anything but bloodshed in return. He’s struggling with his loyalties because he’s not a fan of Black down and his blacker ways of doing battle. His loyalty gets tried further when the ex-prince comes into the mix because he and Dow are obviously enemies, and Craw had been around Calder since he was a child and helped raise him in some respects.<br /><br />And we also have Bethod’s son, “Prince” Calder who’s no longer a prince now that his father is dead and Dow holds the crown in the north. His wife is being held captive to ensure his good behavior, but this guy sort of reminds me of Jalan from Mark Lawrence’s Red Queens War. He’s kind of a slippery bastard, more likely to lie to you than not. He’s also a self-professed coward and truly terrible in a sword fight – he’s mostly just trying to survive the battle.<br /><br />Final Score: 14/15<br /><br />Characters:<br />Beck is sort of a jerk to the rest of the trainees he’s grouped with, he’s convinced he’s the baddest new recruit and is thirsty to win his name. I didn’t really know if I liked him all that much, he was pretty immature, quick to a fight, and there wasn’t much in the way of redeeming factors. However, watching him try to navigate through his first battle does make you sympathize with him, and he turns into a rather tragic character.<br /><br />Gorst is OBSESSED with Finree and it plays a major part in his story arc, he has a lot of inner dialogue each time he speaks with her, which is pretty creepy but also funny at points. He’s a very tired and bitter person, he resents his current station as Observer for the king, what he really wants is to be reinstated to his old position which he lost in disgrace some time before the events of this book. As the book goes on he gets more and more bitter and depressed and fed up with his life.<br /><br />Calder is fairly cowardly and instead of trying to fight Black Dow head on, he’s trying to sew seeds of disloyalty in Dow’s thralls. Trying to get each of them to turn against Dow one by one by whispering things in their ear, some true, some not. He has a wife, but he’s not faithful – although he says he loves her and does think of her a lot. He has a stressed relationship with his half brother, who’s more of a warrior than a thinker.<br /><br />Finree is extremely ambitious and it almost seems like no matter how high she gets, she just wants to go higher. She’s very bold and very brave, enduring some battle scene hardships the way some warriors would. She has to stand up to Black Dow at one point and manages to make demands and keep eye contact – which a lot of Dow’s own men can’t do. She has a lot of good ideas and strategies, but she’s ignored due to her gender and she finds it infuriating. She and her husband have an interesting relationship, she’s never quite certain how she feels about him, although he seems fairly besotted with her. She’s definitely the backbone of the relationship and does seem to at least care about her husband even if it’s not the most passionate romance.<br /><br />Final Score: 12.5/15<br /><br />World Building:<br />Much the same of the first trilogy, so to keep this brief – The Union is “civilized” with those fancy mother fuckers eating with forks and having holes where the poop gets flushed away. The north is full of warring clansmen, it’s colder, it’s harsher, and it breeds a hard society.<br /><br />Final Score: 12.5/15<br /><br />Pacing:<br />This is a much faster paced book than the original trilogy, and it’s a stand alone so it sort of has to be. There’s no real build up, you’re thrown into it from almost the very beginning. There’s a battle scene in this were I was listening with furious intensity, I was so into it. If I had been reading the physical book I would have been flying through it.<br /><br />Final Score: 14/15<br /><br />Writing:<br />The writing continues to be amazing in this book, Abercrombie has a way of using repeated phrases that really hammer home certain personality traits or overall takeaway messages and instead of being annoying, they are deftly done and work well. He uses a straight forward writing style that’s sprinkled with metaphor and simile, not being flowery, but creating interesting imagery that doesn’t slow the pace.<br /><br />Final Score: 13.5/15<br /><br />Originality:<br />Again, this isn’t exactly the most trope busting book that’s out there, but I couldn’t care in the least because of how strong the plot and characters are. What was unique about this story was a battle scene done unlike any other I’ve read, so it definitely earned some points from me there.<br /><br />Final Score: 11/15<br /><br />Personal Enjoyment:<br />I really liked this one, I think my favorite Abercrombie book is still Before They Are Hanged, but, this one is a very strong book that I really enjoyed listening to – the audiobooks are just superb.<br /><br />Final Score: 9/10<br /><br />Audience:<br /><br />For people who have read First Law<br />For people who want more twisted characters with grey morals<br />For people who want a lot of action<br />For people who like low level magic<br />For people who like a lot of violence and bloodshed<br />For people who like characters struggling with depression<br />For people who like seeing two sides of a war<br />For people who like fast paced books<br /><br /><br />Final Score: 87/100</span>
  <a data-text-id="1609866328394206437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5720233352456708694">It's been a really long time since I read the First Law books and several years since I read Best Served Cold, so I started off a little lost on this book. I didn't remember what had happened between Black Dow and the Bloody Nine, I didn't really remember Calder or Gorst so I ended up doing some Wikki reading trying to catch back up.   <span id="freeText5720233352456708694" style="display:none">It's been a really long time since I read the First Law books and several years since I read Best Served Cold, so I started off a little lost on this book. I didn't remember what had happened between Black Dow and the Bloody Nine, I didn't really remember Calder or Gorst so I ended up doing some Wikki reading trying to catch back up. Once I got it all straight I really enjoyed it. I actually found a few people that were worth "cheering for" (at least by Abercrombie's standards) and the big scene at the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Dow vs Calder  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> had me actually feeling nervous about the outcome. Totally didn't see that ending coming - which is great, I love it when I can't see a major plot point coming. Although I did see this coming a mile away <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Whirrun dying - which made me sad, I liked him  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Anyway - overall I liked it. Bayaz is still a giant asshole, but I found more people in this book to be likeable (vs the characters in the First Law books). Not a good place to start though if you haven't read any of the other books in the series.</span>

<div id="review_1065659450" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner"><img alt="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551272804p2/3481302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1065659450?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eon ♒Windrunner♒  " href="/user/show/3481302-eon-windrunner">Eon ♒Windrunner♒  </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1065659450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7347144895118454123">War in all its misery. Did you expect anything else? This book is as Abercrombie as it gets. As The Bloody Nine would say, you have to be realistic about these things.<br/><br/>The story takes place a couple of years after the first law trilogy (read it first!) and centers mostly around a three day battle between the Union & the North. There are quite a few of the characters we have come to love present, but sadly, also a few key ones that have gone back to the mud in between books. I mention them only be</span>
  <span id="freeText7347144895118454123" style="display:none">War in all its misery. Did you expect anything else? This book is as Abercrombie as it gets. As The Bloody Nine would say, you have to be realistic about these things.<br /><br />The story takes place a couple of years after the first law trilogy (read it first!) and centers mostly around a three day battle between the Union &amp; the North. There are quite a few of the characters we have come to love present, but sadly, also a few key ones that have gone back to the mud in between books. I mention them only because I was really hoping to read more of them. Abercrombie has a knack for writing characters that you just want to keep on reading about. In some of his other books I have found the plot to sometimes stall a bit, but the strength of the personalities he has captured on the paper always pulls him through and thoroughly makes up for any shortcomings in the story-line. The plot did not need any assistance this time round though.<br /><br />I must mention the excellent sequences where multiple POV characters are used in battle, with a change in the POV triggered by death, and POV changing from the victim to the perpetrator each time. Superb.<br /><br />The only thing I disliked was the death of my fav character in this book. Oh, and also the tying up of the different characters story-lines which seemed slow after the huge final battle. Necessary, but slow.<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7347144895118454123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827195906" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827195906?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvana" href="/user/show/666003-silvana">Silvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=fyeahfantasy">fyeahfantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827195906" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14950381829622257136">I may write a longer review when I have time. Conclusion, this book is a perfect fictional war account. I read a lot of nonfiction combat memoirs etc and this book has the same quality. It's got the specifics, troops movement, tactics and strategies, politics among and between each participants, heroics and cowardice and what I appreciate the most, the facts (and musings) that war is not glamorous at all. Songs can sung about heroes and countries but at the end, it's all about standing side by s</span>
  <span id="freeText14950381829622257136" style="display:none">I may write a longer review when I have time. Conclusion, this book is a perfect fictional war account. I read a lot of nonfiction combat memoirs etc and this book has the same quality. It's got the specifics, troops movement, tactics and strategies, politics among and between each participants, heroics and cowardice and what I appreciate the most, the facts (and musings) that war is not glamorous at all. Songs can sung about heroes and countries but at the end, it's all about standing side by side with your comrades. 'We lucky few, we band of brothers.' Shakespeare knew his shit, alright. I really really admire the Northmen because they got that kind of spirit. Which is the only good thing that could ever be resulted from a war. <br /><br />I am still unsure about the ending, it pretty much solves most of the arcs but I still feel something missing. It is not a let down oh hell no I love the stark realism of what's left after the fighting is over, but.... I don't know. Maybe I still want more explanation on why X did that in the circle (trying to avoid spoilers here) . I was surprised but still puzzled on the motive.</span>

<div id="review_2033900130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2033900130" />
    <a title="Vladimir Ćeha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49589906-vladimir-eha"><img alt="Vladimir Ćeha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515358074p2/49589906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2033900130?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vladimir Ćeha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vladimir Ćeha" href="/user/show/49589906-vladimir-eha">Vladimir Ćeha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2033900130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7785294471319592722">Finally.<br/><br/>Yes, that’s how I feel after finishing this book. I loved the First Law trilogy, but Heroes just fell flat for me. In spite of the title, the novel is not about heroes, in fact Abercrombie never misses a chance to remind us that his characters are not honorable men. Everything was different in the distant past, when people knew what they were fighting for, but nothing remains of that time, only rock formations that are aptly named Heroes, and where most of the action takes place today. I</span>
  <span id="freeText7785294471319592722" style="display:none">Finally.<br /><br />Yes, that’s how I feel after finishing this book. I loved the First Law trilogy, but Heroes just fell flat for me. In spite of the title, the novel is not about heroes, in fact Abercrombie never misses a chance to remind us that his characters are not honorable men. Everything was different in the distant past, when people knew what they were fighting for, but nothing remains of that time, only rock formations that are aptly named Heroes, and where most of the action takes place today. It is an ironic setting for our scheming and shallow characters, who are not heroes at all. Did I say there is nothing heroic about them?<br /><br />And it goes on and on like that, becoming very repetitive and predictable. There is hardly any magic, although Bayaz is present, playing the puppet master. Of course, he represents the Union, while on the other side there is Ishri, a powerful Gurkish Eater. But what do they do with their powers? They play with gunpowder for a while and that’s it. <br /><br />It felt so anticlimactic, like I wasn’t reading epic fantasy, but a novel with a watered-down taste of fantasy. And it is really just about a stretched out battle, that takes place over the course of three days, with Abercrombie repeating how the scuffle between the Union and the North makes no sense whatsoever. No one wins in the end, there are only losers on both sides.<br /><br />I could get behind this notion if the characters are convincing enough, if there is some sort of catharsis in the end. However, as I previously mentioned, everyone here reminded me of Glokta, Bloody Nine and others from the First Law trilogy. What is more, they came across as cheap imitations. I felt nothing for them. Gorst was irritating, Black Dow’s potentional was not fully realized, but what annoyed me most was this bunch of cliched characters from the North. I think I know how Abercrombie comes up with them: he gives them a generic nickname, as well as a catchphrase which they can repeat over and over again, some kind of physical disability, and voila, he can send them on their merry way.<br /><br />It is interesting how supportive characters were actually better, Beck for example. His story arc made sense to me. To end on a more positive note, I will also say that the novel is gritty and very realistic in its portrayal of war. There are traces of black humor, but nothing memorable really. It was a long story that I struggled to finish, and after being too generous with Half a King, which I gave four stars in spite of its flaws, I’m gonna go ahead and give this one a three star rating. Abercrombie can do so much better than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7785294471319592722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_906748878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906748878" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2314568-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463021489p2/2314568.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906748878?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/2314568-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2314568-steve?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2314568-steve?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2314568-steve?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906748878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1557307674339891309">The premise of the book is very straight-forward: the Union and the Northmen are fighting a war over a narrow strip of borderland, and “The Heroes” is the setting of a long and bloody three-day battle. The title is a play on words, and without spoiling anything, the hilltop setting named “The Heroes” and the violent battle there bring out the heroic in men on both sides.<br/><br/>“The Heroes” follows Abercrombie’s previous titles chronologically, so if you haven't read the other books yet, start with “The</span>
  <span id="freeText1557307674339891309" style="display:none">The premise of the book is very straight-forward: the Union and the Northmen are fighting a war over a narrow strip of borderland, and “The Heroes” is the setting of a long and bloody three-day battle. The title is a play on words, and without spoiling anything, the hilltop setting named “The Heroes” and the violent battle there bring out the heroic in men on both sides.<br /><br />“The Heroes” follows Abercrombie’s previous titles chronologically, so if you haven't read the other books yet, start with “The Blade Itself” and work your way through. You’ll be glad you did. Overall, the series is very good, and it’s gotten better. Abercrombie has made steady progress as a writer. His writing has grown more technically sound and is tighter overall. Words are worth more. The voices of his characters have become more sure, and his ability to juggle multiple characters and an increasingly-numbered cast of supporting characters has vastly improved.<br /><br />Abercrombie’s improved ability to weave character arcs is displayed in “The Heroes”. This was a slight problem in the initial trilogy, in which many characters came through as flat, and only a handful of characters grew through the storylines. With “The Heroes,” Abercrombie juggles a huge cast and keeps up with most all of them, whether major or minor; and they all have well-conceived character arcs, fleshed out from start to finish. While some of his peripheral characters remain flat, used to flavor various scenes, Abercrombie has raised most of them to three-dimensional status, with wants and desires, and small character arcs of their own.<br /><br />Abercrombie is sticking with the same general direction as the previous books, and his readers should recognize why: he’s still world-building, even here in the fifth novel set in this universe, and following the overarching events as they happen. He continues to build and progress his world with ever-increasing details in both characters and settings. “The Heroes” is a great story, focusing on very flawed men (and women) making decisions (both good and bad) in desperate situations, and the consequences of following those decisions.<br /><br />Overall, “The Heroes” is a very satisfying read, and an outstanding addition to the world of the First Law.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1557307674339891309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_302434714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302434714" />
    <a title="Ryan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1500718-ryan"><img alt="Ryan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238846167p2/1500718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302434714?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan" href="/user/show/1500718-ryan">Ryan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302434714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10132535713339722387">When asked what sort of music I liked to listen to, I answered "grunge" for years after it was fashionable to do so. I think most of us can name a musician or band that we loved in high school, one that we listened to well past pop culture's imposed expiration date. Perhaps most of us can even recall the time when we realized that our tastes were no longer fashionable. Eventually, we have to see what's hip "today," and I suspect that the same holds true for fantasy.<br/><br/>When I was a young man, listen</span>
  <span id="freeText10132535713339722387" style="display:none">When asked what sort of music I liked to listen to, I answered "grunge" for years after it was fashionable to do so. I think most of us can name a musician or band that we loved in high school, one that we listened to well past pop culture's imposed expiration date. Perhaps most of us can even recall the time when we realized that our tastes were no longer fashionable. Eventually, we have to see what's hip "today," and I suspect that the same holds true for fantasy.<br /><br />When I was a young man, listening to night mice scurrying in the ceiling of my parents' basement as I read about dungeons and dragons, the big names on my bookshelf, repeated in innumerable sequels, were Robert Jordan, the Terry Surnames, and even David Eddings. George R.R. Martin was about to release <i>A Game of Thrones</i>, which changed all of the rules.<br /><br />"Most men would rather deny a hard truth than face it," said Tyrion, and I suppose that was true for me as well. Times had changed. <br /><br />I eventually gave up on fantasy, or at least stopped looking for new authors to read.<br /><br />Robert Jordan passed away before he could finish his work, fantasy readers began to ask whether it was even worth it to even start "The Wheel of Time," and a writer I'd never even heard has taken over the series (I think Sanderson's done well so far). I grew out of Terry Brooks and Goodkind in much the same way that grunge fans grew out of the genre when Creed became popular. For what it's worth, I still read "The Wheel of Time" and I still buy Pearl Jam's albums.<br /><br />I eventually gave up on fantasy, but I eventually returned to it as well.<br /><br />So what was hip in SFF by the time I'd finished university?<br /><br />(YA, it turns out.)<br /><br />I suppose I've spent the last few years answering this question. It was during this time that I discovered China Miéville, began reading Neal Stephenson, and even William Gibson latter day masterpieces (all of whom translate better to adults than teens I think).<br /><br />One of SFF's hippest writers might be Joe Abercrombie, but it's taken me a while to pick up one of his books. Like many SFF writers today, Abercrombie is clever. He plays with our expectations, characterizing Whirrun and his "Father of Swords" as a force to be reckoned with and leaving us wondering who could pose a threat to him. In the end, Abercrombie is confident that everyone paid to imagine decapitation, and every page between us and decapitation eventually starts to feel like a tease.<br /><br />What sometimes seems incredibly unfashionable in today's SFF is romance. As a self conscious teen I would have said no romance is fine, and as an adult, I am more than content to do without the adolescent romance and chosen one motifs. However, I do sort of miss the righteous hero and the quest. We live in a world that is depressing enough. Is it too much to hope for a romantic escape from the mundane?<br /><br />In <i>The Heroes</i>, Abercrombie does not offer the romance of a quest. Instead, he offers us a hill. <br /><br />People are buried beneath it. And it will decide the victor in a campaign between the North and the Union -- a campaign that is really just a prelude to negotiations anyway. Neither side can really claim to have "right" on their side. Neither side can claim to have a heroic leader, either. Instead, readers can sit back and wait for decapitation. Between then and now, we are offered gritty, grizzled workers and corrupt leaders.<br /><br />What part of this is an escape from the world we live in?<br /><br />Having said that, Abercrombie does a remarkably fine job of achieving what he has set out to do. I also think that he enjoys writing fantasy more than any other author that I have read. I felt that I could see him smiling on the other side of every page (of my Kindle), which I found mostly endearing (sometimes disturbing).<br /><br />But ultimately, I didn't find this violent and bloody pastiche, ironically titled <i>The Heroes</i>, very endearing. I was raised on Eddie Vedder's (in retrospect, I see that they're) self-righteous lyrics.<br /><br />Consequently, I'm starting to feel that Lev Grossman is writing the best fantasy right now. It challenges and satisfies conventions remarkably well. But I still have others to read. I'll probably read either Lynch's <i>Lies of Locke Lamora</i>, Priest's <i>Boneshaker</i>, or Rothfuss's <i>Wise Man's Fear</i> next, all of which were published recently, so are probably just pastiche. Wish me luck.<br /><br />*<br /><br />-Favorite latter day Pearl Jam song: "Unthought Known."<br />-Favorite latter day Eddie Vedder song: "Guaranteed." That's right, I followed him into his solo career as well.<br />-Favorite "Wheel of Time" novel? <i>The Dragon Reborn</i><br />-Favorite latter day "Wheel of Time" novel? <i>Towers of Midnight</i> (the plot advances)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10132535713339722387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144297300?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=war">war</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144297300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15377299529649570233">There must be something about the The First Law trilogy. Because while I loved those three books, I can't say I felt the same enthusiasm for Joe A's other book Best Served Cold or this one, The Heroes. It was very hard for me to give this book a low rating, but I had to be honest; I just didn't enjoy it.<br/><br/>Despite being packed with action-filled battle scenes, it was a struggle to get through this book without nodding off within the first thirty minutes each time I picked it up. That's probably why</span>
  <span id="freeText15377299529649570233" style="display:none">There must be something about the The First Law trilogy. Because while I loved those three books, I can't say I felt the same enthusiasm for Joe A's other book Best Served Cold or this one, The Heroes. It was very hard for me to give this book a low rating, but I had to be honest; I just didn't enjoy it.<br /><br />Despite being packed with action-filled battle scenes, it was a struggle to get through this book without nodding off within the first thirty minutes each time I picked it up. That's probably why it took me so long to finish.<br /><br />Since the book covers events over a three day period during a war, I thought this format would give Abercrombie a better chance to really showcase his characters, and make them shine the way he did with the Bloody Nine and Sand Dan Glokta in the First Law trilogy. Instead, I found them mostly dull and uninteresting. Perhaps this had something to do with the fact so many points of view are being covered in this book, but none of them really stood out as having a distinct voice. Contrast this to Glokta, whom Joe A. supplied with a very recognizable personality and thought process. <br /><br />Hmm, I don't know. Maybe I just liked the First Law too much and expectations started out too high for this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15377299529649570233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1207936924" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1207936924" />
    <a title="James &#39;Eagle&#39;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10740280-james-eagle"><img alt="James &#39;Eagle&#39;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411315962p2/10740280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1207936924?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James &#39;Eagle&#39;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James &#39;Eagle&#39;" href="/user/show/10740280-james-eagle">James &#39;Eagle&#39;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780575083837" href="/book/show/9919092-the-heroes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10740280-james-eagle?shelf=2010-s-fantasy">2010-s-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10740280-james-eagle?shelf=must-read-fantasy">must-read-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1207936924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1014459296383762239">This book is breathtaking. The ultimate sum of it's parts, 'The Heroes' is a perfect display of Abercrombie at his absolute best: grim, brutal, vivid, real, and intensely moving. I fell in love with this novel early on and that feeling still hasn't gone away even after I turned its last page. It's a story that made me want to finish work as soon as possible so I could go back to it. An experience that had me thinking about it hours after it ended. It is a phenomenal ride, one that has pushed thi</span>
  <span id="freeText1014459296383762239" style="display:none">This book is breathtaking. The ultimate sum of it's parts, 'The Heroes' is a perfect display of Abercrombie at his absolute best: grim, brutal, vivid, real, and intensely moving. I fell in love with this novel early on and that feeling still hasn't gone away even after I turned its last page. It's a story that made me want to finish work as soon as possible so I could go back to it. An experience that had me thinking about it hours after it ended. It is a phenomenal ride, one that has pushed this into the ranks of my favourites of all time.<br /><br />What I love about this novel (the same reason I loved 'Best Served Cold') is that it doesn't need to dwell on worldbuilding. The necessary stage-setting has all been dealt with in the original 'First Law' trilogy allowing Abercrombie to take the characters we've already come to know, put them in a separate independent story, and focus so finely on it that it has the amount of depth, realism, and time to make this story extremely satisfying. <br /><br />I feel like I learn something new every time I read an Abercrombie novel. He goes into his work with so much heart and intelligence with lessons and analyses of all types of human nature, inviting you to think of the nature of humanity when the odds are completely stacked against them. It is an incredibly human novel in an inhuman world and the characters that inhabit it are beautifully, achingly real.<br /><br />The military tactics shown indicated a real amount of research into Medieval battles, and the map of the ever fluctuated regimental tides with each passing day really aided the reader in gaining a full understanding of the battle in hand. There was so much thought put into the ins and outs of this novel. From the personal character-shaking stories of Gorst and Shivers, to the world-changing actions of Bayaz, First of the Magi. Each individual thread felt like all part of a plan for the world of the First Law, and it was incredibly exciting to see the world develop. <br /><br />Gorst, Calder, and Craw were the three characters who received the most attention in the novel, and it shows clear skill that Abercrombie is able to evoke empathy with multiple viewpoints in this novel. You get a grand sense of how this battle affects everyone, not just the select few. With important moving choices being made by other characters such as Tunny, Finree, Beck, and Whirrun. Each individual stands out as a fully-realised character in a horrific situation. Some deal with it far better than others, but all of their reactions are entirely real and believable.<br /><br />The sense of combat anarchy is achieved through selective description and a rapid writing-style during the most intense battle sequences. This served to place the reader directly in the midst of the battle. You feel like you are right in the middle of it all, with people fighting and dying all around you. It is seriously intense. And there are moments of pure brilliance like with the chapter 'Casualties' which follows a number of different people caught in the battle, the viewpoint swiftly moving to whoever killed them as you jump from sorry victim to sorry victim and witness the full extent of this battle's horrific brutality. If this doesn't show you the utter shit that is war, no novel will.<br /><br />The themes were full explored and the genre-bending that Abercrombie is so known for is subtle, not in your face. Heroism, self-preservation, redemption, ambition, desire are ripe throughout and make this story what it truly is, an absolute masterpiece.<br /><br />So, yes, I loved it. How could I not?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1014459296383762239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_458669901" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/458669901" />
    <a title="Hanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9653496-hanne"><img alt="Hanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1381183161p2/9653496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/458669901?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hanne" href="/user/show/9653496-hanne">Hanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575083851" href="/book/show/9300804-the-heroes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9653496-hanne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer458669901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9684645656301687528">I've been reading a lot of Abercrombie lately - one a month for the past 5 months to be exact. One more to go and (sad face) it'll be over for a while. I hope Abercrombie is writing fast!<br/><br/>This book contains more of what Abercrombie is absolutely brilliant at:<br/>Gritty, dark but oh so real. This book tells the story of war: the Union and the Northmen have been in a cat-and-mouse-war for a while, but the council needs their army elsewhere and commands a short end to this war. We'll get three days of w</span>
  <span id="freeText9684645656301687528" style="display:none">I've been reading a lot of Abercrombie lately - one a month for the past 5 months to be exact. One more to go and (sad face) it'll be over for a while. I hope Abercrombie is writing fast!<br /><br />This book contains more of what Abercrombie is absolutely brilliant at:<br />Gritty, dark but oh so real. This book tells the story of war: the Union and the Northmen have been in a cat-and-mouse-war for a while, but the council needs their army elsewhere and commands a short end to this war. We'll get three days of war. <br />Abercrombie shows the victories, the failures, the astonished reactions to new weapons. He writes about the 'heroes' but about the 'cowards'. One of the young lads in this war, son of a famous Named Man, always dreamt of becoming a famous fighter, but he chickens out of his first attack and hides in a cupboard.<br /><br /><br />And yet, what Abercrombie does so well is to balance all that heavy stuff with a lot of humour. Black humour usually, but he regularly makes me chuckle nonetheless. There are many moments i could have chosen, but i'm copying the one on the invention of sliced bread (parts of it, that is).<br /><br /><i>"I sliced the bread thin, d'you see?" (Whirrun slicing bread with his sword)<br />"Sliced bread?" Wonderful turned away from the black valley to watch him. "Can't see it catching on, can you?"<br />Whirrun ignored 'em. "Then when I got two cut, I trap the cheese between them and there you have it!"<br />‘Bread and cheese.’ Yon weighed the half-loaf in one hand and the cheese in the other. ‘Just the same as I’ve got.’ <br />Whirrun sighed. ‘Have none of you no vision? A whole new thing. A forging of the humble part of bread and cheese into a greater whole. I call it … a cheese-trap.’ Whirrun took a dainty nibble from one corner. ‘Oh, yes, my friends. This tastes like … progress…” <br />(...)<br />Whirrun pointed at her harply with his whole new thing and the cheese fell out into the unlit fire. Wonderful near fell over from laughing. Yon snorted so hard he blew bread out of his nose. <br />Whirrun frowned at his two flapping slices of read. "Don't think i wrapped it tight enough."</i><br /><br /><br />Last but (definitely) not least, in this book Abercrombie shows again his brilliant character building. So many characters to cheer for. Too many to all put down here, so i'll just stick to my absolutely favorites:<br /><br />Finree, daughter of the marshall:<br /><i>Finree: "They're idiots!"<br />Hal: "Have you ever noticed that everyone's an idiot but you?"<br />Finree: "You see it too?"</i><br /><br />But there's also Calder (a thinker, not really a fighter) and Craw (an experienced Named Man):<br /><i>Calder: "Guess he couldn't beat the Union without my mighty sword-arm."<br />Craw: "What's his plan? Cut it off and throw it at 'em?"</i><br /><br /><br />This book is not for the faint-hearted. It's about war and all the little things that go along with war. It's a really good book, but personally i still prefer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2315892.Best_Served_Cold" title="Best Served Cold by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">Best Served Cold</a>. Maybe just a little too much war in this one. I preferred the revenge plotting over these wargames, which seems so ... pointless. But i guess that might actually be the point after all. <br /><br /><br /><i>“The truth is like salt. Men want to taste a little, but too much makes everyone sick.” </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9684645656301687528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2122617311" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2122617311" />
    <a title="Nils | nilsreviewsit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52846007-nils-nilsreviewsit"><img alt="Nils | nilsreviewsit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560928352p2/52846007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2122617311?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nils | nilsreviewsit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nils | nilsreviewsit" href="/user/show/52846007-nils-nilsreviewsit">Nils | nilsreviewsit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575099579" href="/book/show/9300798-the-heroes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2122617311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3664741106632079366">Abercrombie you madman! How did you do it? How did you write another glorious book that I can't help but love?! Well it's easy I guess, you went and wrote a book all about a battle spanning over three days. Anyone who knows me knows I love battles, so really this book was made for me!<br/>🏹<br/>Let's sum the book up in emoji's - ⚔️⚔️😂😂😂⚔️⚔️😵😵😭😭😯<br/>🏹<br/>As you can see there are a lot of swords here! My favourite characters in this were definitely the Northmen - particularly Craw and his small crew. I loved how Cr</span>
  <span id="freeText3664741106632079366" style="display:none">Abercrombie you madman! How did you do it? How did you write another glorious book that I can't help but love?! Well it's easy I guess, you went and wrote a book all about a battle spanning over three days. Anyone who knows me knows I love battles, so really this book was made for me!<br />🏹<br />Let's sum the book up in emoji's - ⚔️⚔️😂😂😂⚔️⚔️😵😵😭😭😯<br />🏹<br />As you can see there are a lot of swords here! My favourite characters in this were definitely the Northmen - particularly Craw and his small crew. I loved how Craw internally debated every decision he made, tried to keep his friends alive and always tried to do the right thing even when he didn't know what that was. The friendship he had with his band was just the best. Every time they were around a fire, bantering with each other, I bloody loved it! Abercrombie writes so detailed and realistically that I felt I was sitting by the fire with them, I was laughing at the jokes with them. I loved that!<br />🏹<br />Another favourite character was Corporal Tunny. He always brought some light comic relief to all the heavy battle scenes. I loved how Tunny tried very hard to do as little work as possible, and the way he took the piss out of his recruits was hilarious!<br />🏹<br />Gorst was a pretty cool character too - he was a beast on the battlefield!<br />🏹<br />The battle scenes in this were just EPIC, it was honestly some of the best blood and gory scenes I've ever read! I mean at one point a character was using his shield as an umbrella to stop the blood raining down on him! 😱 The scenes were also written so realistically, and often humorously. Abercrombie had a beautiful way of conveying how confusing battles can be for soldiers, how boring it is to wait around for orders, how the consequences of generals making mistakes was devastatingly high. What I loved was how he showed both sides of war - the sheer waste of life that war causes, how pointless it is, but also how a lot of people used to prosper from it and gain names for themselves.<br />🏹<br />That's the thing I love about this author, not only does he entertain and amuse, he makes you think, he makes you question morals.<br />.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3664741106632079366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_335660613" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/335660613" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/335660613?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781409130772" href="/book/show/9300810-the-heroes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer335660613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12032012108108466422">Three days. Three days to secure a throne, Three days to make a name. Three days to become a hero. Three days of blood.<br/><br/>The Heroes covers 3 days of war between The Union and The North. After years of smaller battles and sieges and move and countermove, the closed council has grown impatient and the Union generals are ordered to hurry things up and march head on into the enemy and bring the war to a conclusion.<br/><br/>This book was action packed! I mean condensing 500 to 600 pages into 3 days of plot is n</span>
  <span id="freeText12032012108108466422" style="display:none">Three days. Three days to secure a throne, Three days to make a name. Three days to become a hero. Three days of blood.<br /><br />The Heroes covers 3 days of war between The Union and The North. After years of smaller battles and sieges and move and countermove, the closed council has grown impatient and the Union generals are ordered to hurry things up and march head on into the enemy and bring the war to a conclusion.<br /><br />This book was action packed! I mean condensing 500 to 600 pages into 3 days of plot is no mean feat and Abercrombie does it in style. Fair to say a lot happens in those three days. From large scale battles churning the mud, to bloody skirmishes, to individual acts of murder and feats of heroism. On top of that is the internal politics and intrigue on both sides with a cast of characters that will see some old faces from previous books along with a host of new ones. <br /><br />Abercrombie skilfully weaves the old and the new together in such a way that had me intimately involved in the motives and dreams of his masterfully crafted personalities and the audio narrator, Steven Pacey, brought these to life in a way that I’m not sure reading alone could have achieved.<br />Having said that I was torn between enjoying the audio narration and having the ability to highlight on the Kindle because the quotable quotes in this book just keep coming with Abercrombie’s usual blacker than Black Dow sense of humour. This is a dark, gritty, bloody story. But there is also under the gore a commentary on war that is more cynical than preachy. Abercrombie highlights the fact that the winners of a war, if there are any, are usually the ones with the most blood on their hands. That in war there is often fine line between hero and mass murderer, if such a line exists at all. After all, as Cosca from the previous book might point out, “Why can’t a man be both?” Is there a difference between murdering a man in peace time and killing a man just because he wears a different uniform to yours? How does a good man decide what is, “The right thing to do,” when faced with the choice between conscience and expediency? <br /><br />At the end of the day we all have a date with The Great Leveller and the dead know, whether you are Hero or Coward, in the end, both “go back to the mud.” And often, the advantage of being a Hero, is you get to jump the queue.<br /><br />5 stars – and my favourite to date. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13521459.Red_Country" title="Red Country by Joe Abercrombie" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Country</a> here I come.<br /><br />Some of my favourite characters<br /><br /><b>Black Dow King of the North</b><br />“As if Black Dow’s name and his grin weren’t threats enough, he’d made sure they were shored up with plenty of steel. A long, grey sword leaned against Skarling’s Chair on one side, an axe on the other, notched with long use, in easy reach of his dangling fingers. Killer’s fingers – scuffed, and swollen, and scarred at the knuckles from a lifetime of the dead knew what dark work.”<br /><br /><b>Calder - 2nd Son of the previous King of North</b><br />“It's not easy is it? Being a great man's son. You'd thought that would come with all kinds of advantages - with borrowed admiration, and respect. But it's only as easy as it is for the seeds of a great tree, trying to grow in its choking shadow. Not many make it to the sunlight for themselves.” <br /><br /><b>Craw - Named Man - likes doing "The right thing to do."</b><br /> "I need someone I can count on, Craw, and you do things the old way. You’re a straight edge, and there ain’t many left."<br /><br /><br /><b>Deep and Shallow - killers come philosophers</b><br /><br /><i>Calder</i> ‘A man should have some, eh, Deep?’<br /><i>Deep</i> ‘Some what?’<br /><i>Calder</i> ‘Principles.’<br /><i>Deep</i> ‘Oh, I’m a big, big, big believer in ’em. My brother too.’<br /><i>Shallow</i> Shallow took a quick break from furiously picking his fingernails with the point of his knife. ‘I like ’em with milk'<br /><br /><b>Shivers - Also known as Black Dow's dog</b><br />They said Shivers did tasks for Black Dow too black for his own hands.<br /><br /><b>Whirrun - Famous hero of many a bard's song.</b><br />‘What kind of a bloody hero don’t wear bloody armour?’<br />‘Armour …’ mused Whirrun, licking a finger and scrubbing some speck of dirt from the pommel of his sword, ‘is part of a state of mind … in which you admit the possibility … of being hit.’<br /><br /><b>Colonel Gorst - Ex King's guard, now disgraced and demoted to King's Observer, a killing machine and all round ninja.</b><br />I made myself guilty of mass murder so I could be proclaimed innocent of incompetence. Sometimes they hang men for this type of thing, and sometimes they applaud.<br /><br /><b>Corporal Tunny - longest serving non-commissioned officer(and contraband peddler) in the army </b><br />‘Corporal Tunny, sir, standard-bearer of his Majesty’s First Regiment.’<br />Mitterick frowned. ‘The same Tunny who was made colour sergeant after Ulrioch?’<br />Tunny puffed out his chest. ‘The same, sir.’<br />‘The same Tunny who was demoted after Dunbrec?’<br />Tunny’s shoulders slumped. ‘The same, sir.’<br />‘The same Tunny who was court-martialled after that business at Shricta?’<br />And further yet. The same, sir, though I hasten to point out that the tribunal found no evidence of wrongdoing, sir.’<br /><br /><b>Finree</b><br />‘Ordeal? I’ve almost forgotten about it already! My father suggested that I act as though this is just another day. Then, perhaps it will be one. Any other day I would spend feverishly trying to advance my husband’s interests, and therefore my own.’ She grinned sideways. ‘I am venomously ambitious.’<br /><br /><b>Bayaz the First of the Magi</b><br />‘Knives,’ muttered Calder, ‘and threats, and bribes, and war?’<br />Bayaz’ eyes shone with the lamplight. ‘Yes?’<br />‘What kind of a f___g wizard are you?’<br />‘The kind you obey.’<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12032012108108466422" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill"><img alt="Paul O&#39;Neill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462480730p2/17331573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1261541358?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul O&#39;Neill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul O&#39;Neill" href="/user/show/17331573-paul-o-neill">Paul O&#39;Neill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17331573-paul-o-neill?shelf=top-11-books">top-11-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1261541358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6203926180249765748">Probably my favourite read of 2018! <br/><br/>A great cast of characters, gripping action and military strategy. <br/><br/>I’m just going to say it, Abercrombie is the best builder of characters I’ve ever read. Even better than Stephen King. That’s probably as high an accolade I can give any writer! <br/><br/>The audiobook version is also highly recommended. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('l1pXERLj35eYSGZmDn13N+mpvccnZHBV1AyRFI3dJUYhi8oE1OVhKr+QBiPBJdHuxqzy3ZHSODAhp1CRiWOwSg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4vQ2m57xkmeGajQomAa1Q0xTjWONNCgwdb7tarlLJ3NUJauOWPcs2qGyVG1XXhOaY1bCeTuCYFWAFSzvvfWyfw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/276660.Joe_Abercrombie">About Joe Abercrombie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11406623564774718118">Joe Abercrombie was educated at Lancaster Royal Grammar School and Manchester University, where he studied psychology. He moved into television production before taking up a career as a freelance film editor. During a break between jobs he began writing <i>The Blade Itself</i> in 2002, completing it in 2004. It was published by Gollancz in 2006 and was followed by two other books in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/43644-the-first-law' rel='nofollow noopener'><i>The First Law</i> trilogy</a></span>
  <span id="freeText11406623564774718118" style="display:none">Joe Abercrombie was educated at Lancaster Royal Grammar School and Manchester University, where he studied psychology. He moved into television production before taking up a career as a freelance film editor. During a break between jobs he began writing <i>The Blade Itself</i> in 2002, completing it in 2004. It was published by Gollancz in 2006 and was followed by two other books in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43644-the-first-law" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>The First Law</i> trilogy</a>, <i>Before They Are Hanged</i> and <i>Last Argument of Kings</i>. He currently lives and works in London with his wife and daughter. In early 2008 Joe Abercrombie was one of the contributors to the BBC Worlds of Fantasy series, alongside other contributors such as Michael Moorcock, Terry Pratchett and China Mieville.</span>

Caught in one feud too many, he’s on the verge of becoming a dead barbarian – leaving nothing behind him but bad songs, dead friends, and a lot of happy enemies. \n\nNobleman Captain J<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7631654158717441433\" style=\"display:none\">Logen Ninefingers, infamous barbarian, has finally run out of luck. Caught in one feud too many, he’s on the verge of becoming a dead barbarian – leaving nothing behind him but bad songs, dead friends, and a lot of happy enemies. \n\nNobleman Captain Jezal dan Luthar, dashing officer, and paragon of selfishness, has nothing more dangerous in mind than fleecing his friends at cards and dreaming of glory in the fencing circle. But war is brewing, and on the battlefields of the frozen North they fight by altogether bloodier rules. \n\nInquisitor Glokta, cripple turned torturer, would like nothing better than to see Jezal come home in a box. But then Glokta hates everyone: cutting treason out of the Union one confession at a time leaves little room for friendship. His latest trail of corpses may lead him right to the rotten heart of government, if he can stay alive long enough to follow it. \n\nEnter the wizard, Bayaz.
